1 ROAD IMPACT STUDY
1.1 Introduction
This document corresponds to the Road Impact Study that has been prepared in the context of the
Environmental Impact Study of the Project “Clay Extraction Mining Development Project for
Production of Rare Earth Concentrate” (hereinafter the Project), which analyzes the potential
negative externalities of the execution of this Project on the relevant road network.
The objective of this work is to present the public roads surrounding the Project that will be used as
access route for its transportation actions, expose the flow that the Project will generate towards it, and
review updated background information that characterizes the traffic flows of the roads to be used.
Together with the above, the present study seeks to develop a founded analysis of the effect
of traffic
during the most restrictive phase of vehicle concentration of the Project, evaluating whether it generates alteration
significant in consideration of literal b) of article 7 of DS 40 “the obstruction or restriction to the free
circulation, connectivity, the significant increase in travel times” due to transit
regular of the Project.
1.2 Justification
Projects that have trip-generating characteristics, such as the present one, could present
certain externalities on the adjacent public roads, being of greater magnitude in the vicinity of the
Project and of lesser magnitude as we move away from it.
Among the negative externalities or impacts possible to generate on public roads, it is considered, for
For example, the increase in concurrent, directional and functional conflicts of vehicular flow and the
increase in traffic congestion.
1.3 Objectives
The general objective of this study is to identify and quantify the road impact that could be caused by
Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for the Production of Rare Earth Concentrate,
proposing measures to mitigate it.
Likewise, the following specific objectives have been considered:
• Characterize the current physical-operational situation of the Road Influence Area
• Characterize the Current Road Demand of the Road Influence Area.
9
==================================================================================
PAGE 11
==================================================================================
Annex 4-3 Road Impact Study
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
• Estimate the vehicle demand of the Project.
• Model the most relevant intersections and road sections of the road network to be used by the
Project.
1.4 Methodology
To address the possible road impacts of the Project, the criteria established in the Manual were used.
of Highways (Directorate of Roads, 2022) and the Regulation on Mitigation of Impacts to the Transportation System
Local Mobility derived from Urban Growth Projects (MTT, 2019). Likewise, they are considered
aspects contemplated in the Guide for the Description of Land Transport Action in the SEIA and the
Guide for the Description of the Area of Influence in the SEIA (SEA, 2017).
Next, the methodological aspects contemplated in the development of this present are described.
report:
1.4.1 Initial Definitions
The initial definitions included aspects such as the Area of influence, Temporal cut, Rates of
vehicle growth and Periodization.
The general criterion to define the Area of Influence of this component is given by the alternatives of
vehicular routes that could be used by the Project as part of its various actions.
For this purpose, the Guide for the Description of the Area of Influence in the SEIA has been considered (Exempt Resolution
N°0423 of the Executive Directorate of the SEA), dated April 26, 2017.
The Temporal Cut refers to identifying the year where the highest concentration of flow is generated-attracted.
Project vehicle.
Regarding vehicle growth rates, they allow updating and projecting vehicle flows. In
In particular, rates recommended by the Ministry of Social Development and Family (2022) were used.
To periodize, continuous vehicle measurements were developed for 13 hours/day (between 7:00 a.m.
and 8:00 p.m.) at relevant intersections within the area of influence of the Project1. From them
identified the critical periods of the transportation network. To periodize, all the
movements made at the measurement points.
1 As indicated in the Highway Manual in Volume 6 (MOP, 2022), continuous flow measurements must be carried out
during the 8 hours of greatest demand. However, in the absence of further information, the Manual proposes carrying out counts of
transit for 12 hours between 7:30 and 7:30 p.m.
10

Annex 4-3 Road Impact Study

Rare Earth Concentrate
1.4.2 Characterization of the Current Situation
1.4.2.1 Road Offer
The evaluation of the road supply allowed us to know the current functioning of the road system.
transportation in the
Project influence area. For this, basic information was collected in the field regarding each one.
of road segments and intersections, in order to systematize their main physical characteristics.
operational.
In the field campaign, information was recorded on all the routes that make up the area of ​​influence.
From the operational point of view, the following antecedents were recorded: regulation of intersections,
maximum speed allowed, directions of traffic, signaling and demarcation, flow measurement
vehicle per period, among others. From the physical point of view, the following were recorded: number and use of tracks, width
of road (median and shoulder), length of roads or axes between stop lines, type and state of
pavement, among others.
1.4.2.2 Current Road Demand
In order to characterize the vehicular demand on the roads that will be used by the Project, it was considered
information from different sources, valid and current:
 Continuous flow measurements carried out in August and November 2022.
 Continuous measurements recorded in August 2018.
The continuous vehicle measurements were carried out on a business day of the normal season and
considered the recording of all permitted movements at gauged intersections, between
07:00 and 20:00, totaling 13 hours of continuous recording. The data was updated to the year 2023
through the application of vehicle growth rates. Detailed information about each point of
control, as well as location, schedules, sources, type of measurement, treatment and statistical analysis, are
It is available in section 4.2.1 of this report.
1.4.2.3 Accident rate
To identify conflictive sectors from an operational and physical point of view, information was collected
through different sources: Transparency Law to the National Traffic Safety Commission
(CONASET), CONASET Geospatial Information Portal and Proactive Transparency of Carabineros of Chile,
regarding vehicle accidents recorded on the routes that will be used by the Project. The period
considered in the analysis was between the years 2010 and 2022. The information collected includes the frequencies
annually, the location, main causes and types of accidents.
11
==================================================================================
PAGE 13
==================================================================================
Annex 4-3 Road Impact Study
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
1.4.3 Diagnosis of the Current Situation
Once the entire area of analysis was registered, a diagnosis was prepared with the purpose of identifying
those critical and/or conflictive points from the operational and physical point of view.
1.4.4 Estimation of Transportation Demand
The transportation demand was estimated for the construction and operation stages of the Project,
considering these as the most restrictive scenarios in terms of vehicle concentration; and for
two Scenarios: Base and with Project2. The transportation demand for the Base Scenario was estimated
projecting to the year of cut, the vehicular flow observed in the current situation (post treatment with rates
of growth). In the Scenario with Project, the demand was obtained by incorporating, into the base scenario
(same cut-off year), trips induced by the Project.
1.4.5 Definition of the Road Offer
The definition of the road supply considered the Base and Project Scenarios. The road supply for the situation
base corresponded to the existing one, plus the infrastructure financed by other sources and that will be found
in operation after one year of simulation. For the Scenario with Project, the flow considered in the
Base Scenario, adding the vehicular flow induced by the Project.
1.4.6 Intersection Modeling
A modeling and subsequent simulation of the Current Scenario, Base and with Project was developed to
those intersections of relevance within the transportation network. This required calibration and
adjustment of the model to be used, in this case SIDRA. Indicators of degrees of saturation, delay
average and tail length.
1.4.7 Service Level Analysis of Track Sections
The Service Level Analysis Methodology describes the operating conditions of a section of road in
terms of factors such as speed and time traveled, operating costs,
onals and freedom of
perform maneuvers, among other variables. The above was developed considering what was established in the
Highway Manual (MOP, 2022). And its objective was to analyze whether the incorporation of the flow generated by
The Project in an unfavorable condition will generate a significant impact on the level of service of
stretches of track, and as a consequence a significant increase in travel times of the
users of public roads.
2 Two Base scenarios were considered, one for each stage of the Project (Construction Base and Operation Base) and four
With Project scenarios, also for each stage, but adding assumptions of vehicular flow distribution
generated by the Project.

1.4.8 Conclusions and recommendations of the study
From the analysis of the main results of the study, some conclusions are made, in addition to
propose road safety recommendations for the Project's transportation actions and in the case of
If necessary, voluntary action, management or road improvement measures.
2 BACKGROUND OF THE PROJECT
2.1 Description and location of the Project
The Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for the Production of Rare Earth Concentrate
consists of the construction and operation of a mining site, along with a waste processing plant.
Regolith type material, with a strong presence of clays. Regolith is material from a rock
highly weathered, with the presence of lanthanides adsorbed on clay minerals. The lanthanides
There are 15 elements: lanthanum (La), cerium (Ce), praseodymium (Pr), neodymium (Nd), promethium (Pm), samarium (Sm),
europium (Eu), gadolinium (Gd), terbium (Tb), dysprosium (Dy), holmium (Ho), erbium (Er), thulium (Tm), ytterbium (Yb) and
lutetium (Lu), yttrium (y) and scandium (Sc) are also added, which are widely known as
Rare Earths.
The Project considers developing three (3) extraction zones (ZE Luna, ZE Victoria Norte, ZE Maite), one
disposal area for waste and processed clays (ZD Neptuno), a processing plant (the
Plant), a topsoil collection area (ZAV), electrical transmission line and construction and
improvement of roads to access different areas. Additionally, the implementation of
temporary works corresponding to work facilities, for the construction and enabling of the
Project works.
The plant will have a capacity to process up to 320 tons/hour of concentrate clays.
Rare Earths.
Administratively, the Project is located in the communes of Penco and Concepción, Province of
Concepción, Biobío Region.
13

EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of

2.2 Project access paths
The Project is located mainly in the commune of Penco and some sectors in the extreme north of the
commune of Concepción, Biobío Region. For access from/to public roads, it is evaluated to use
two accesses:
 Access 1 - Route 150 Km 5, Penco - Lirquén Route.
 Access 2 - Route 152 Km 71 Itata Route.
Access from route 152 will allow entering the Processing Plant from the existing public road.
and then from there connect to the different areas of the Project through the use of roads
internal. On the other hand, the existing access on route 150 will allow direct access to both the plant
processing, as well as the extraction and disposal areas of the Project.
14
==================================================================================
PAGE 16
==================================================================================
Annex 4-3 Road Impact Study
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
To reach the aforementioned accesses it is necessary to use the aforementioned routes Route 150 and Route 152,
complete
ment to these roads, and to connect with points of origin or destination of transportation actions to
generated by the Project, other access roads are required, such as Route 154, Av. Pdte. George
Alessandri, Av. Costanera, Av. El Manzano, among others, which will allow connection with the main
sources of inputs, personnel, destination of waste, as well as transportation points for the mineral
processed (Puerto de Lirquén).
The following figure shows the location of the Project in relation to the surrounding public roads.
Figure 2-2. Access roads
Source: GAC
2.3 Project Schedule
The Project will have a construction phase that will begin in January 2026 and contemplates a
duration of 25 months. The operational phase is estimated to begin in January 2028, with a 6-year extension. The
The closing phase is expected to take place in January 2034, with an end date 12 months after the start.
It is necessary to specify that the dates indicated correspond to estimates and are subject to both

2.4 Vehicular Flow Generated by the Project
Below is the estimated vehicle flow for the Project in its construction phases,
operation and closure. Both vehicular movements within the Project area and
trips to/from public roads, the latter are the relevant ones for this road study.

The vehicular flow generated during the construction phase corresponds to the transportation of personnel, supplies
construction, supplies for domestic use and food, machinery, water (industrial and consumer
human), fuels as well as waste and others, this for the different works and sectors of the Project.

Annex 4-3 Road Impact Study
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
According to the previous table, during the construction phase of the Project, 123,257
trips, of which 43,661 trips are to/from public roads. Of these, 5,408 trips will occur during
the peak month (month 4 construction phase), which is equivalent to 199 daily trips.
2.4.2 Operation Phase
The operation phase considers operating activities of the Project sectors, therefore, it is
They generate flows linked to inputs, mineral movements, products, personnel and waste.
The following graph shows the annual vehicle flow of the operation phase, associated with road traffic.

2.4.4 Conclusions of the vehicular flow generated by the Project
In accordance with the reviewed background, it is assumed that the Project will have a construction phase with a
maximum vehicle concentration of 199 daily trips linked to public roads. For its part, the phase
operational, has the highest vehicle concentration of the phase (public roads), during year 3 of
her, with a maximum accumulation of 166 daily trips. A maximum of 81 is expected for the closing phase
daily trips to destinations or origins where the use of public roads is required. The above indicates
that the phase with the highest vehicle concentration of the Project will be the construction phase. Likewise, year 3
of the operation phase is considered the most restrictive within its phase.
According to the Project schedule, available in section 2.3, the construction phase is
will develop during the years 2026 and 2027, where, in terms of projection (growth of the park
vehicular), the year 2026 is considered the most restrictive of the phase. For its part, year 3 of the
Operation will take place during the year 2030.
3 INITIAL DEFINITIONS
3.1 Definition of the area of influence
The Area of Influence has been defined considering the public routes that connect the Project with each
of the origins and destinations of the trips generated and attracted by it, considering the different actions
of transportation, the above taking into account the Area of Influence Guide in the SEIA, Exempt Resolution
N°423 of the Executive Directorate of the SEA (2017).
The parts, works and actions that make up the Project are located in the communes of Penco and Concepción,
in the Biobío Region. In particular, the roads that make up the Area of Influence and that allow access
The different areas of this correspond to the following:
 Route 150, between Av. El Manz
year and Route 154
 Route 152, between Route 150 and El Cabrito Underpass.
 Av. El Manzano, between Route 150 and Puerto Lirquén Access.
 Access road to Puerto Lirquén, between Av. Manzano and the checkpoint.
 Route 154, between Route 150 and Av. Pdte. Jorge Alessandri Rodríguez.
 Av. Pdte. Jorge Alessandri Rodríguez, between Route 154 and Av. Costanera.
 Av. Costanera, between Av. Pdte. Jorge Alessandri Rodríguez and Av. Great Britain.
The Area of Influence is schematized graphically in the following figure:

3.2 Temporary Cut
According to the vehicle flow history of the Project reported in section 2.4, the phase of
construction will be the one that concentrates the greatest amount of vehicular flow, constituting, therefore,
in the worst evaluation scenario. In particular, a maximum of 199 trips are expected during the year 2026.
daily to/from public roads. For the operational phase, the year that concentrates the highest vehicular flow
of the Project, corresponds to year 3 (2030), where a maximum of 166 daily trips are expected.
Considering the above, it is contemplated to use the year 2026 as a temporary cut-off, corresponding to the
first year of the construction phase; and the year 2030, which corresponds to the third year of the
operation, which correspond to the most restrictive scenarios of both vehicle concentration of the
Project (2026), as with greater concentration of the operational phase (2030).

3.4 Periodization
The concept of periodization is directly linked to the concept of congestion. Congestion produces,
as a main effect, that resource consumption in vehicle operation and trip utility
perceived by users vary depending on the flow.
On roads where vehicles can circulate in free flow conditions, their operating cost is
directly proportional to the volume of traffic. However, when the vehicle volume (in terms
level, composition and distribution by direction of traffic) begins to affect the speed of travel
of vehicles is called congestion, the existing linearity between operating costs and costs is lost.
the traffic volume. Consequently, the need arises to work with a different approach,
incorporating as an analysis tool the definition of periods representative of the total hours
of the year.
Considering the above, for periodization purposes, the record of flow measurements was used
continuous vehicle type (between 07:00 and 20:00, completing 13 hours of continuous registration) inside
of the Area of Influence, whose individual report is found later in section 4.2.1.
For the analysis, the sum of all the vehicular flows measured within the Area of
Influence, and its transformation to “Equivalent Vehicles” using the factors of
equivalence recommended in MESPIVU.
Table 3-2. Equivalence factors
Type of Vehicles Equivalence Factor
Light Vehicles and Taxis 1.00
Collective Taxi 1.35
Taxi buses 1.65
Buses 2.00

Table 4-13. Road characterization intersection No. 3
Intersection No. 3
Observations
It corresponds to two segregated Y-shaped junctions between Route 150 (north and south access) and the branches of
access/egress from Av. El Manzano, which allows connection with Puerto Lirquén. Priority regulation is
given by the vertical sign give way (RPI-1) present at the eastern access of the junction and which grants priority
of way to direct movements on Route 150.
Route 150 corresponds to a road with two bidirectional carriageways, with two lanes in each direction, as well as thirds.
tracks for speed change from/to the exit and/or egress branches. Your road surface is asphalt
and is in good condition. The roads are 10.5 m wide (3.5 m per lane)
segregated by a continuous double line, and immediately south of the junctions, with new jersey barriers (this
due to the presence of a signalized pedestrian crossing). Both the vertical signs and the demarcations are
They are in good condition.
Connecting branch Route 150 – Puerto de Lirquén (junction
east) connects with the east road of Route 150
and allows you to exit from this and also access the trunk road heading north. It has two segregated tracks
by a central island with sills. The presence of zebra crossing type demarcations, outside the norm, is recognized
because the width of its demarcations is not continuous. The presence of an egress route is recognized
additional, which allows connection with the residential sectors to the east of the junction, it also connects
internally with the Puerto de Lirquén branch.

4.1.2.5 Intersection N°5: Roundabout Route 150/ Route 154 (General Bonilla)
Table 4-15. Road characterization intersection No. 5
Intersection No. 5
Observations
It is configured as a three-level link, with the routes for direct movements uneven (lower routes
154/ 146 and above Route 150/ Av. San Juan Bosco) and a level roundabout with 8 branches. Nearby you can see
also exclusive tracks for turning movements between approaches. The priority regulation is given by
the vertical Give Way signs (RPI-1), present on the access branches to the roundabout and on the lanes
exclusive for turning, giving priority to movements within the roundabout lanes and on direct roads
uneven. This link is inserted in the urban context of Concepción, which is why it has a high
vehicular flow.
Route 154 has a bidirectional double carriageway with two lanes in each direction. This configuration extends to
east of the roundabout where its role changes to Route 146. Its road surface is concrete at the west access
to the roundabout and asphalt, on the western access. Direct movements can be executed without interference on
the west-east axis (uneven). For turning movements, third and fourth contiguous tracks are added
to both carriageways, where they allow movement along an exclusive lane to the right, or entering and exiting
to the level roundabout. Pedestrian walkways are observed for crossing the roads at both accesses to the link.
Route 150 has a bidirectional double carriageway, with two lanes in each direction. Their roads are contiguous in the
north access to the roundabout, but at the south access, where it acquires the name of Av. San Juan Bosco, they are segregated
through a large median and the eastern road now has a section with 4 lanes, where the 2 exterior ones
They allow movements on the roundabout and turning on the exclusive runway. Like the east – west axis,
direct movements are without interference, but through the upper step of the link.

Intersection No. 7
Observations
It is configured as a roundabout with three lanes and 4 branches, three of which are segregated into different
roadways, to isolate the entry and exit movements of the roundabout. The roads that join the roundabout are
Av. Costanera (east-west axis) and Av. Great Britain (north-south axis). The priority regulation is given by
the vertical sign give way (RPI-1) where priority movements take place on the inside lanes
of the roundabout.
Av. Costanera corresponds to a road with a bidirectional double carriageway, with two lanes in each direction. Its roads are
They are segregated by a 5 m wide median, which increases in size as you approach the roundabout.
Its road surface is made of concrete and is in good condition.
Av. Great Britain has a bi-directional single carriageway, with one lane in each direction, which are segregated, in the
roundabout, due to the presence of a central island. Its road surface is made of concrete. The south access to the roundabout
also receives on behalf of Av. Great Britain, but this access is not consolidated, it does not have
priority regulation signal and only has a folder of concrete wheels in the connection wedge
to the roundabout.
Both the central islands and the external sidewalks of the roundabout have double wave barriers. The state
of these elements and vertical signage are in good condition. For their part, the
demarcations are in fair condition.

4.4 Diagnosis of the Current Scenario
The Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for the Production of Rare Earth Concentrate,
It will be located in the commune of Penco and a small one in the extreme north of the commune of
Conception. The Project will have two accesses to two roads, the first through an existing road.
which connects with Km 5 of Route 150 (access to the CEMARC landfill), the second corresponds to
through the enabling of four accesses located on both sides of Km 71 of Route 152. The area
of road influence considered the structuring public routes that provide connectivity to the
Project with its different sources of inputs, machinery, personnel and/or product transportation
finished, making possible the transport actions to be carried out by it.
In general, the roads that make up the road influence area are in a good state of conservation.
most of its elements. Routes 150, 152, 154, Av. El Manzano, Av. Pdte. Jorge Alessandri
Rodríguez and Costanera Avenue have asphalt and/or concrete in good condition.
Failures are only recognized in a section of Av. El Manzano close to the access to the Port of Lirquén where
Cracks or potholes can make normal vehicle traffic difficult. Same situation happens with
elements associated with vertical signage, which are observed to be in good condition, only
Specific elements present flaws linked to maintenance problems or lack of elements. In
Regarding the demarcations, in general in good condition, shortcomings linked to problems of
wear or lack of elements (mainly Av. El Manzano and Access to Puerto Lirquén).
At the intersection level, the following crossings were reviewed: Route 150 with the access road to the Port of
Lirquén (Av. El Manzano), Av. El Manzano with Av. La Marina, Route 150 with access to the landfill
CEMARC (Access to Project Km 5 Route 150), General Bonilla Roundabout (Routes 150/ 154), Roundabout

Av. Pdte. Jorge Alessandri Rodríguez (Carriel Sur) and Rotonda de Av. Costanera with Great Britain. In a way
In general, the reviewed intersections are in good condition, with geometry consistent with vehicle traffic.
heavy, adequate visibility and good condition of vertical signage, present only exceptions
specific details such as the regular status of the vehicle folder at the intersection of Av. El Manzano and Av. La Marina;
the lack of vertical priority regulation signs at some intersection entrances on Av. El Manzano,
with Av. La Marina, with the access branch to Route 150 and at the southern access to the Av. Costanera roundabout
with Av. Great Britain; and intersections with horizontal signaling elements (demarcations) with
wear problems or lack of priority legends (crossings of Av. El Manzano and Route 150 with
Access to CEMARC).

the Project, where the busiest periods were identified

Light vehicles, followed by Trucks and Buses. Regarding the rush hour, according to the analysis of the flows
continuous type vehicular, this takes place during Punta Mañana between 07:30 and 08:30 h.
Finally, a review of accident statistics was carried out on the road sections that are part of
of the Area of Influence. Noting that there is a moderate to low accident rate, and that the
The majority of the causes of accidents correspond to the driver's recklessness. The most typologies
recurring correspond to collision. There is a marginal number of accidents associated with
road deficiencies, all in the section of Route 150, being particularly linked to traffic of
animals on public roads.
5 ANALYSIS OF THE BASE AND PROJECT SCENARIO
5.1 Road Offer of the Base Scenario
As part of the analysis of the base scenario, information was collected on road projects to be executed in
the area of influence. The above was carried out based on the request for public information within the framework
of the Law on Transparency of the Public Function and Access to Information of the Administration of the
State (Law No. 20,285). In addition, it was complemented with information available in Concesiones MOP and in
public access web portals.
It should be noted that the request and response letter from the Authority are delivered in Appendix 2 of the
present report.
113
==================================================================================
PAGE 115
==================================================================================
Annex 4-3 Road Impact Study
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
5.1.1 Road Projects
Consultations were made to the authority about the existence of road projects within the area of
influence of the Project. Consultation No. AM010T00044227 was made to the MOP Highway Directorate to
the following ways:
- Route 150
- Route 154
- Av. Costanera (URB-452)
- Av. Pdte. Jorge Alessandri Rodríguez (URB-450).
According to the authority's response, routes 150, 154 and Av. Costanera do not have projects
current or pending roads in the sections within the road influence area of the Project. Av. Pdte. George
Alessandri Rodríguez (URB-450) has no current projects, but is in an initiative
financing (BIP N°40038838-0) called “Improvement of Av. Jorge Alessandri Sector: Trébol de
Highway – Costanera”, which is in the pre-feasibility stage, waiting to be tendered to
mid-2023.
5.1.1.1 Second North Access Concession to Concepción
According to what is indicated on the website of the Ministry of Public Works, the project is located in the
region of Ñuble and Biobío, and, in general terms, consists of the improvement, construction, maintenance
and exploitation of both pre-existing works and new works included in the concession.
This with the aim of improving the technical standard and service levels of the route, and, consequently,
guarantee safety and comfort conditions for its users.
The new concession of the Northern Access to Concepción considers a total extension of 96.1 km, which includes
75.1 km of Route 152 and 14.1 km of Route 158, plus a new 6.9 km route, which will connect
Direct Route 152 with Route 146.
Among the main milestones of this project are 40.5 km of route rectification and 36.9 km
of pavement rehabilitation, in addition to 22.4 km of widening berms and 4.6 km of third lanes.
On the other hand, 12 new walkways will be developed, 22 new stops with lighting and circuit
pedestrian area, a new general services area and 2 new sales areas for typical products and a
new emergency care area.

private located in the area close to the Project. The reviewed projects were evaluated

projects are running simultaneously.

in the Project, the year 2026 and year 2030.

5.3 Project Demand Estimation
5.3.1 Peak Hour Demand Estimation
Keeping in mind the
revised daily vehicle demand in section 2.4, which indicated that the most
restrictive period of the Project, in terms of flow concentration, will be month 4 of the construction phase (2026),
when a maximum flow of 199 daily trips is expected; also that the restrictive situation that is generated
for Year 3 of the operational phase (2030), it is the one with the highest concentration within the phase, where it is expected
a maximum of 166 daily trips. In both situations, the vehicular flow for the peak hour will be defined.
To construct the estimate, vehicle flow measurements will be considered as valid background information.
continuous revised for the area of influence of the Project, specifically those of PC N°6: Roundabout Route
150/ Route 154 General Bonilla (See section 4.2.1.6), according to said capacity, the busiest hour
recorded a total of 7,676 vehicles/h, which represents approximately 9.9% of the total flow measured between
7:00 a.m. and 8:00 p.m. (77,775 daily vehicles measured). Considering the above, for the purposes of this
study, the following restrictive assumptions will be assumed, depending on the type of vehicle recognized for
the phases to analyze:
 Peak hour vehicle flow for the transportation of personnel (buses and light vehicles) will consider
an hourly concentration of 50% of the daily vehicle flow of the Project.
 Peak hour vehicular flow for the transportation of supplies, waste and others, in general
trucks, will consider a concentration of 20% of the daily vehicle flow of the Project.
The above assumes a much more restrictive concentration than that registered within the area of
influence, thus assuming an unfavorable flow evaluation scenario.
Next, the estimate of the Project's vehicular flow for the theoretical peak hour is provided.
taking as reference the assumptions described above, both for the most restrictive scenario of
vehicle concentration of the Project (month 4, construction phase), as for the most restrictive scenario
of the operational phase (Year 3). The estimate was generated from the daily travel frequency of the
Project from/to public roads, for each type of vehicle, reviewed in Table 2-2 for the phase of
construction and in Table 2-3 for the operation stage of the Project.

5.4 Diagnosis of Base Scenario and with Project
Based on the background provided by the Owner and the analysis carried out on the Development Project
Clay Extraction Miner for the Production of Rare Earth Concentrate, it is estimated that, for the
more restrictive situation in terms of vehicle concentration in the construction phase,
specifically month 4 Year 1 (2026), the Project will present a maximum concentration of 48 trips in
rush hour. The same flow of 48 trips at rush hour will present the operational phase of the Project in its
most restrictive condition, the one that corresponds to year 3 (2030). The previous calculations were carried out
on restrictive concentration criteria during rush hour. From the different access routes,
associated with the origins/destination of the transportation activities, vehicular flow of the Project,
distributed in the different sections of the area of influence.
It is important to mention that the Project will have two entrances where entry/exit will take place.
of vehicles, the first existing, is located at Km 5 of Route 150, which corresponds to the current access
to the CEMARC landfill, and the second to be executed corresponds to four accesses to be located in both
sides of Km 71 of Route 152 (projected). It should be noted that these are evaluated
independent in the present study, since restrictive scenarios of 100% of the flow to
generate or attract through one access (Km 5 Route 150) and then through the other (Km 71 Route 152).
Regarding the existence of road projects in the area of influence of the Project, in accordance with the
information sent by the Road Departments, there are no current or pending projects for the
roads within the area of influence. Therefore, it is expected that the roads will not modify their geometry and
current dimensions, that is, the situation of the Base Scenario and With Project, will be similar to the situation
current.
The following chapters address the analysis of road simulation, including background information.
mentioned, for the quantification of impacts in relation to the consumption of road resources through
SIDRA modeling and Service Level analysis in the sections of the road influence area. The objective,
is to quantify the impact that the Project could have on adjacent public roads, and in the case
If necessary, evaluate some measure aimed at neutralizing it.

The modeling was developed using the SIDRA INTERSECTION 9.1 software, considering that the

6.1.1 Modeling Scenarios
The modeled scenarios are the following:
 Current Scenario (EA 2023): Scenario built based on the vehicular flows collected in the
year 2022, updated to 2023 based on the vehicle growth rates reported in the
numeral 3.3.
 Base Construction Scenario (EBC 2026): Flows are projected from 2023 to 2026 from
of the vehicle growth rates available in section 3.3. This year is considered as
temporary cut because it concentrates the largest vehicular flow of the Project (Month 4 phase
construction).
 Scenario With Construction Project A (ECPCA 2026): Similar to the base construction scenario
2026, but the Project flows from month 4 of the construction phase are incorporated (higher
vehicle concentration of the Project), contemplating the entry/exit through the access located in
Route 150 Km 5 (Access to CEMARC).
 Scenario With Construction Project B (ECPCB 2026): Similar to the base construction scenario
2026, but the Project flows from month 4 of the construction phase are incorporated (higher
vehicle concentration of the Project), contemplating the entry/exit through the accesses
alternatives located on Route 152 Km 71.
 Base Operation Scenario (EBO 2030): Flows are projected from 2023 to 2030 from
of the vehicle growth rates available in section 3.3. This year is considered as
temporary cut because it concentrates the largest vehicular flow of the phase (Year 3 operational phase).
 Scenario With Project Operation A (ECPOA 2030): Similar to the base operation scenario 2030,
but the Project flows from year 3 of the operational phase are incorporated (greater concentration
vehicle of the phase), contemplating the entry/exit through the access located on Route 150 Km 5
(Access to CEMARC).
 Scenario With Operation B Project (ECPOB 2030): Similar to the 2030 operation base scenario,
but the Project flows from year 3 of the operational phase are incorporated (greater concentration
vehicle of the phase), contemplating the entry/exit through the alternative accesses located in the
Route 152 Km 71.
Finally, the period with the highest vehicle concentration in the study area was modeled according to
with the periodization carried out in section 3.4.

The traffic indicators obtained from the modeling were:

 Degree of Saturation, X (%): Equivalent to vehicle flow
icular (veh/h) that passes along a track, divided by
its capacity (veh/h). It is worth mentioning that a track that has a higher degree of saturation
90% is classified as saturated.
 Average Queue Length, LC (veh): Equivalent to the average of the queues formed on a runway.
 Average Vehicle Delay, VEH DP (sec): Equivalent to the average time it takes for vehicles to
vehicles passing through an intersection.
 Effective Capacity, Qo (veh/h): Equivalent to the ratio between the total flow of the intersection with the
highest degree of saturation of the intersection entrances.
Reserve Capacity, QR (veh/h): It is equal to 90% of the capacity of a runway minus the flow that
circulates through it. On the other hand, the reserve capacity may be zero (0 veh/h) as indicated
in the following expressions:

heavy (trucks and buses).

According to the global results obtained from the modeling of the aforementioned intersections,
stable operation is observed between the Base Scenarios (EBC 2026 and EBO 2030) and With Project
(ECPCA 2026, ECPCB 2026, ECPOA 2030 and ECPOB 2030). No significant increase is detected in
saturation indicators (X), average delays (DP VEH) and queue lengths (LC) as a result of the
incorporation of the Project flow, for any d
and the two accesses evaluated. The maximum saturation
presents the intersection PM N°5: Route 150/Access to CEMARC, which in the Scenario with Project
Operation A 2030 (ECPOA 2030) reaches 89%. It is important to mention that this situation drags
from the baseline scenario, and is not generated by the contribution of the Project, since in the Base Scenario 2030 (EB
2030) there is already an 89% degree of saturation for the aforementioned point, and with the Project there is no
generate significant variations, both for the saturation indicator and for the average delays.
Therefore, it is possible to indicate that the incorporation of the Project's vehicular flow does not cause a detriment
in the operating conditions of the evaluated intersections.

projection of flows through the use of vehicle growth rates
6.4 Modeling Conclusions
According to the analysis of saturation degrees, the highest records are present in the junction
PM N°5: Route 150/ Access to CEMARC, with a current saturation of 69%, which increases to 77% and 89%
for the Base Construction (EBC 2026) and Operation (EBO 2030) scenarios, respectively, as a result of the
growth of the sector's vehicle fleet. The With Project scenarios present similar indications
143
==================================================================================
PAGE 145
==================================================================================
Annex 4-3 Road Impact Study
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
or with marginal variations with respect to the basal condition, with 77% saturation in the scenario of
Construction A (ECPCA 2026) and 79% for the Construction B scenario (ECPCB 2026); and with 89% in
the Operation scenarios (ECPOA 2028 and ECPOB 2028), that is, the flow incorporated by the Project does not
generates variations or its impact is marginal. It is important to mention that this condition
is presented from the baseline scenario (EBO 2030) and is in no case a product of the incorporation of
Project flows,
but rather, by the application of growth rates to flow measurements
current vehicular traffic at the modeled intersections and by the incorporation of environmental projects that
They have RCA approved. The rest of the intersections show their loose operating indicators and
stable between scenarios, without significant variation due to the addition of the Project's vehicular flow.
Based on the background presented, it is possible to affirm that the introduction of the flows
Project vehicles in the worst vehicle concentration scenarios does not generate a detriment to
the operating conditions of the roads in its Area of Influence. And, therefore, it will not affect
linked to literal b) of art 7 of the Environmental Assessment Regulation. In particular, it will not generate
obstruction or restriction to free movement, connectivity or significant increase in travel times
displacement of human groups that use the revised roads.

of Service applying the aforementioned methodology. Particularly for this Project, these
are the following:

7.1.3 Capacity Calculations and Service Levels
The calculation of Service Levels distinguishes between roads with bidirectional single carriageway and roads
highway type (one-way), where the latter is made up of roads with two or more lanes.
circulation in one direction.
The calculation process is based on assigning a generic capacity, defined for certain conditions
circulation ideals and that will be modified by a series of reduction coefficients depending on
the deviation of the particular characteristics of the road under study with respect to the ideal ones.

The service levels for bidirectional roads are as follows:
 Service level A: It is associated with an operating speed of 93 km/h, or higher. Continuously
there is a visibility distance to overtake; traffic volumes reach 15%
of capacity. Under ideal conditions, a service volume of 420 vehicles can be obtained
light per hour, total in both directions. Most overtaking maneuvers
desired
can be done with little or no delay, with the biggest obstacle being vehicles traveling in
opposite direction.
 Service level B: At the maximum vehicle volume limit of this level, many drivers must
control their speeds according to volume conditions. Most drivers
They are affected by other vehicles in the traffic flow, although this effect is still tolerable. The
Operating speeds are 88 km/h or more and volumes can reach 27% of the
capacity if the sight distance is continuous. Volumes of 750 light vehicles are obtained
per hour, totals in both directions, under ideal conditions.
 Service level C: Traffic volumes have a direct effect on travel speeds.
operation, regardless of road alignment, at the limit of this service level, even
With stable flow, operating speeds are 84 km/h or more, and the volume reaches 43% of
the capacity if the sight distance is continuous. Volumes of 1,200 light vehicles are obtained
per hour, total in both directions, under ideal conditions.
 Service level D: There is unstable flow when the operating speed reaches 80 km/h. The
volumes can reach 64% of capacity with continuous speed distance, or 1,800
light vehicles per hour, total in both directions under ideal conditions.
 Service level E: Corresponds to the capacity of the road. Operating speeds fluctuate
around 72 km/h, but can vary considerably. The volumes under conditions
ideal is 2,800 light vehicles per hour.
 Service level F: Represents a forced flow, with unpredictable characteristics. The speeds of
operation are less than 72 km/h, and volumes are below 2,000 light vehicles per hour.

considering three different layout situations, which allow determining the effect of the vehicles
commercials on the capacity of a road. These are:
149
==================================================================================
PAGE 151
==================================================================================
Annex 4-3 Road Impact Study
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
 Flat Terrain: It is that whose horizontal and vertical alignment allows commercial vehicles
maintain operating speeds similar to those of passenger vehicles.
 Undulating terrain: It is that whose horizontal and vertical alignment forces commercial vehicles to
maintain reduced operating speeds in some sectors, lower than that of road vehicles.
passengers. Trucks can operate at normal speeds in short sectors.
 Mountainous Terrain: It is that whose horizontal and vertical alignment forces commercial vehicles to
operate at steady state speed continuously. At the same time the horizontal alignment imposes such
restrictions that passenger vehicles are forced to reduce speed due to this fact.

7.2 Conclusions of Service Level analysis
According to the Service Level analysis in the sections within the Project Road influence area,
none presents a variation in the category between the Base scenarios (EBC 2026 and EBO 2030) and the
With Project scenarios (ECPCA 2026, ECPCB 2026, ECPOA 2030 and ECPOB 2030) as a result of the
incorporation of the Project flows, that is, the introduction of them does not generate changes in the
operating conditions of the sections, this both for the scenario in which the entry is made through the access
153
==================================================================================
PAGE 155
==================================================================================
Annex 4-3 Road Impact Study
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
of Route 150 Km 5, Access to CEMARC (Scenarios With Construction Project 2026 and Operation 2030
Situation A), as for the scenario in which the entry is made through possible future accesses
located at Km 71 of Route 152 (Scenarios With Construction Project 2026 and Operation
2030Situation B). The most restrictive service levels are observed in sections 4 and 5 (Route 150 between
Route 152 and Route 154), which have a type E category, however, this occurs due to the
baseline situation of the route and not a product of the incorporation of the Project flows.
Based on the background presented, it is possible to affirm that the introduction of the flows
Project vehicles in the worst vehicle concentration scenarios (Month 4 construction phase
2026 and Year 3 operation phase 2030) does not generate a detriment to the operating conditions of the roads of the
Area of Influence of this. And, therefore, it will not generate effects linked to literal b) of art 7 of the
Environmental Assessment Regulations. In particular, it will not generate obstruction or restriction to the free
circulation, connectivity or significant increase in travel times of human groups
who use the revised roads.
8 CONCLUSIONS AND RECOMMENDATIONS
From the analyzes carried out throughout the study and according to the Consultant's experience in studies of this
nature, it is possible to comment on the following:
From the analysis carried out on the vehicle flows and demand estimation, it is concluded that, in month 4 of the phase
construction (year 2026) corresponds to the most restrictive, in terms of vehicle concentration, of the
Project, with a maximum daily flow of 48 trips during rush hour. Also, regarding the operation phase,
Year 3 (2030) is the one that concentrates the highest vehicular flow of the phase, with a vehicular flow of 166 trips
daily, equivalent to 48 trips during rush hour. This flow was distributed among the different public routes
d
e access and exit of the Project, considering two evaluation scenarios, the first involves using
only the access located at Km 5 of Route 150 (Access to CEMARC) and the second, the evaluation of using
only future accesses with their possible location at Km 71 of Route 152.
Vehicular flow measurements were carried out at relevant intersections in the road influence area,
identifying that the busiest hour in terms of vehicular flow is the morning rush hour, between
07:30 and 08:30 hours.
Vehicular flow modeling was carried out at relevant intersections in the road influence area,
obtaining as a result that the increase in vehicular flow derived from the Project will not generate a
relevant alteration in the road network. Ruling out, therefore, a significant increase in delivery times.
movement of users of the public routes that the project will use for its transportation activities
transportation. The congestion indicators analyzed are recognized as stable between the scenarios of
basal and Project modeling, in addition to being loose and far from the practical thresholds of
saturation (85%) at all intersections analyzed, except for PM N°5: Route 150/Access to
CEMARC, which presents a saturation degree of 89%, however, it is necessary to emphasize that this

condition is presented from the baseline scenario (EBO 2030) and is in no case a product of the
incorporation of Project flows.
According to the Service Level analysis in the sections within the Project Road influence area,
none presents variation in the category between the base and Project scenarios, due to the
incorporation of the Project flows, that is, the introduction of them does not generate changes in the
operating conditions of the sections. The most restrictive service levels are observed in sections 4
and 5 (Route 150 between Route 152 and Route 154), which have a type E category, however, this
It occurs due to the basal situation of the route and not as a result of the incorporation of Project flows.
Based on the background information collected, it is verified that the Mining Development Project of
Extraction of Clays for the Production of Rare Earth Concentrate will not generate significant alterations
in travel times, ruling out impacts associated with literal b) of Article 7 of D.S 40
(SEIA Regulations). In particular, it will not generate obstruction or restriction to free movement,
connectivity or significant increase in travel times of human groups that make
use of revised roads.
In addition, a series of recommendations are proposed regarding maintaining or improving
the road safety of the access routes to the Project, to be applied once it is approved:
 Full compliance with the national vehicular traffic regulatory law will be required.
 The companies contracted to carry out transportation associated with the Project must have
suitable drivers for the transportation required, requiring driving resumes
of each one.
 Vehicles associated with the Project must respect the established maximum circulation speed
for each road to be used, thus ensuring the safety of pedestrians, cyclists and vehicles other than the
Project that move along the same roads.
 Drivers of vehicles associated with the Project must take special care that the
surrounding vehicular traffic.
 The project trucks must conform to the dimensions established in DFL 850/1998
of the MOP. In the eventual case of transporting materials that, due to their size and/or weight, involve
excess of the indicated measures, the corresponding authorization will be requested from the Directorate of
Roads and the security measures to be adopted in each case will be agreed.
 Both in the construction and operation stages, the trucks will comply in all
moment, the regulations regarding maximum weights, according to their axle configuration (Decree No.
158/80 of the MOP).
 In the event that the Project requires the transportation of dangerous substances, the trucks
this
and/or contractor vehicles, must comply with the provisions of D.S. No. 298/1995 of
Ministry of Transport and Telecommunications, mainly regarding the measures of
associated security and the documents necessary for the transit of vehicles with said
elements.
